   583	
   584	I. Introduction
   585	
   586	Table of Contents
   587	1. Introduction
   588	
   589	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
   590	
   591	Chapter 1. Introduction
   592	
   593	Introduction
   594	
   595	This is the Linux Standard Base Work In Progress 20030621 . An implementation
   596	of anything in this document may not claim to be an implementation of the Linux
   597	Standard Base until such time as the feature moves into the Linux Standards
   598	Base Specification.
   599	
   600	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
   601	
   602	Purpose
   603	
   604	The Linux Standard Base (LSB) defines a system interface for compiled
   605	applications and a minimal environment for support of installation scripts. Its
   606	purpose is to enable a uniform industry standard environment for high-volume
   607	applications conforming to the LSB.
   608	
   609	The LSB defines a binary interface for application programs that are compiled
   610	and packaged for LSB-conforming implementations on many different hardware
   611	architectures. Since a binary specification must include information specific
   612	to the computer processor architecture for which it is intended, it is not
   613	possible for a single document to specify the interface for all possible
   614	LSB-conforming implementations. Therefore, the LSB is a family of
   615	specifications, rather than a single one.
   616	
   617	The LSB is composed of two basic parts: A common specification ("generic LSB"
   618	or "gLSB") describing those parts of the interface that remain constant across
   619	all implementations of the LSB, and an architecture-specific specification
   620	("archLSB") describing the parts of the interface that vary by processor
   621	architecture. Together, the generic LSB and the architecture-specific
   622	supplement for a single hardware architecture provide a complete interface
   623	specification for compiled application programs on systems that share a common
   624	hardware architecture.
   625	
   626	This document is the generic LSB. It must be used in conjunction with an
   627	architecture-specific supplement. Whenever a section of this specification must
   628	be supplemented by architecture-specific information, this document includes a
   629	reference to the architecture supplement. Architecture supplements may also
   630	contain additional information that is not referenced here.
   631	
   632	This document should be used in conjunction with the documents it references.
   633	This document enumerates the system components it includes, but descriptions of
   634	those components may be included entirely or partly in this document, partly in
   635	other documents, or entirely in other reference documents. For example, the
   636	section that describes system service routines includes a list of the system
   637	routines supported in this interface, formal declarations of the data
   638	structures they use that are visible to applications, and a pointer to the
   639	underlying referenced specification for information about the syntax and
   640	semantics of each call. Only those routines not described in standards
   641	referenced by this document, or extensions to those standards, are described in
   642	the detail. Information referenced in this way is as much a part of this
   643	document as is the information explicitly included here.
   644	
   645	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
   646	
   647	Related Standards
   648	
   649	The specifications listed below are referenced in whole or in part by the Linux
   650	Standard Base. When a specification is referenced in a way that imposes a
   651	requirement (for example, "foo must behave as specified in the XyzzySpec"),
   652	then the relevant requirements of that specification apply as if they were part
   653	of the LSB itself. However, if the LSB refers to a specification without
   654	imposing a requirement, then it is merely a reference and does not add
   655	additional requirements. The LSB may refer to a portion of a specification (for
   656	example, to define a specific function or group of functions); in such cases,
   657	only the explicitly referenced portion of the specification applies.

   817	|libgcc_s  |libgcc_s.so.1   |
   818	+---------------------------+
   819	
   820	Table 1-3. Standard Library Names defined in the Architecture Specific
   821	Supplement
   822	
   823	+------------------------+
   824	|Library   |Runtime Name |
   825	|----------+-------------|
   826	|libm      |See archLSB  |
   827	|----------+-------------|
   828	|libc      |See archLSB  |
   829	|----------+-------------|
   830	|proginterp|See archLSB  |
   831	+------------------------+
   832	
   833	These libraries will be in an implementation-dependent directory which the
   834	dynamic linker will search by default.
   835	
   836	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
   837	
   838	How to Use this Standard
   839	
   840	The complete LSB specification is composed of this generic LSB specification
   841	and the supplemental processor-specific specification for a particular
   842	processor architecture. These two documents constitute a specification that
   843	should be used in conjunction with the publicly-available standards documents
   844	it references. The LSB enumerates the system components it includes, but
   845	descriptions of those components may be included entirely in the LSB, partly in
   846	the LSB and partly in other documents, or entirely in other reference
   847	documents.
   848	
   849	II. Base Libraries
   850	
   851	Table of Contents
   852	2. Libraries
   853	
   854	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
   855	
   856	Chapter 2. Libraries
   857	
   858	An LSB-conforming implementation shall support some base libraries which
   859	provide interfaces for accessing the operating system, processor and other
   860	hardware in the system.
   861	
   862	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
   863	
   864	Interfaces for libstdcxx
   865	
   866	Table 2-1. libstdcxx Definition
   867

   869	|Library:|libstdcxx      |

   872	+------------------------+
   873	
   874	All symbols are in the std:: namespace.
   875

   877	standards.

 10172	
 10173	Data Definitions for libstdcxx
 10174	
 10175	This section contains standard data definitions that describe system data.
 10176	These definitions are organized into groups that correspond to system headers.
 10177	This convention is used as a convenience for the reader, and does not imply the
 10178	existence of these headers, or their content.
 10179	
 10180	ISO C serves as the LSB reference programming language, and data definitions
 10181	are specified in ISO C format. The C language is used here as a convenient
 10182	notation. Using a C language description of these data objects does not
 10183	preclude their use by other programming languages.
 10184	
 10185	III. System Initialization
 10186	
 10187	Table of Contents
 10188	3. System Initialization
 10189	
 10190	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 10191	
 10192	Chapter 3. System Initialization
 10193	
 10194	Cron Jobs
 10195	
 10196	Packages may not touch the configuration file /etc/crontab, nor may they modify
 10197	the files in /var/spool/cron/crontabs.
 10198	
 10199	If a package wants to install a job that has to be executed via cron, it shall
 10200	place a file in one of the following directories:
 10201	
 10202	/etc/cron.daily
 10203	/etc/cron.weekly
 10204	/etc/cron.monthly
 10205	
 10206	As these directory names say, the files within them are executed on a daily,
 10207	weekly, or monthly basis, respectively. See below for the rules concerning the
 10208	names of these files.
 10209	
 10210	 If a certain job has to be executed more frequently than daily, the package
 10211	shall install a file /etc/cron.d/cron-name tagged as configuration file. This
 10212	file uses the same syntax as /etc/crontab and is processed by cron
 10213	automatically.
 10214	
 10215	It is recommended that files installed in any of these directories be scripts
 10216	(shell scripts, Perl scripts, etc.) so that they may be modified by the local
 10217	system administrator. In addition, they must be registered as configuration
 10218	file.
 10219	
 10220	The scripts in these directories have to check, if all necessary programs are
 10221	installed before they try to execute them. Otherwise, problems will arise when
 10222	a package was removed (but not purged), since the configuration files are kept
 10223	on the system in this situation.
 10224	
 10225	To avoid namespace conflicts in the /etc/cron.* directories, the filenames used
 10226	by LSB-compliant packages in /etc/cron.daily, /etc/cron.weekly, /etc/
 10227	cron.monthly, or /etc/cron.d must come from a managed namespace. These
 10228	filenames may be assigned using one of the following methods:
 10229	
 10230	  * Assigned namespace. This namespace consists of names which only use the
 10231	    character set [a-z0-9]. In order to avoid conflicts these cron script names
 10232	    must be reserved through the Linux Assigned Names and Numbers Authority
 10233	    (LANANA). Information about the LANANA may be found at www.lanana.org.
 10234	   
 10235	    Commonly used names shall be reserved in advance; developers for projects
 10236	    should be encouraged reserve names from LANA, so that each distribution can
 10237	    use the same name, and to avoid conflicts with other projects.
 10238	   
 10239	  * Hierarchical namespace. This namespace consists of scripts names which look
 10240	    like this: [hier1]-[hier2]-...-[name], where name is again taken the
 10241	    character set [a-z0-9], and where there may be one or more [hier-n]
 10242	    components. [hier1] may either be an LSB provider name assigned by the
 10243	    LANANA, or it may be owners' DNS name in lower case, with at least one '.'.
 10244	    I.e., "debian.org", "staroffice.sun.com", etc. The LSB provider name
 10245	    assigned by LANANA must only consist of the ASCII characters [a-z0-9].
 10246	   
 10247	  * Reserved namespace. This namespace consists of script names which begin
 10248	    with the character '_', and is reserved for distribution use only. This
 10249	    namespace should be used for core packages only, and in general use of this
 10250	    namespace is highly discouraged.
 10251	   
 10252	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 10253	
 10254	Init Script Actions
 10255	
 10256	Init files provided by LSB applications shall accept one argument, saying what
 10257	to do:
 10258	
 10259	start        start the service                                                 
 10260	stop         stop the service                                                  
 10261	restart      stop and restart the service if the service is already running,   
 10262	             otherwise start the service                                       
 10263	try-restart  restart the service if the service is already running             
 10264	reload       cause the configuration of the service to be reloaded without     
 10265	             actually stopping and restarting the service                      
 10266	force-reload cause the configuration to be reloaded if the service supports    
 10267	             this, otherwise restart the service                               
 10268	status       print the current status of the service                           
 10269	
 10270	The start, stop, restart, force-reload, and status commands must be supported
 10271	by all init files; the reload and the try-restart options are optional. Other
 10272	init script actions may be defined by the init script.
 10273	
 10274	Init files must ensure that they will behave sensibly if invoked with start
 10275	when the service is already running, or with stop when it isn't, and that they
 10276	don't kill unfortunately-named user processes. The best way to achieve this is
 10277	to use the init-script functions provided by /lib/lsb/init-functions.
 10278	
 10279	If a service reloads its configuration automatically (as in the case of cron,
 10280	for example), the reload option of the init file must behave as if the
 10281	configuration has been reloaded successfully.
 10282	
 10283	These executable files must not fail obscurely when the configuration files
 10284	remain but the package has been removed, as the default in [the packaging
 10285	system] is to leave configuration files on the system after the package has
 10286	been removed. Only when it is executed with the [purge] option will [the
 10287	packaging system] remove configuration files. Therefore, you should include a
 10288	test statement at the top of the file, like this:
 10289	test -f program-executed-later-in-file || exit 5
 10290	or take the equivalent action if the init file is not a shell script.
 10291	
 10292	If the status command is given, the init script will return the following exit
 10293	status codes.
 10294	
 10295	0       program is running or service is OK           
 10296	1       program is dead and /var/run pid file exists  
 10297	2       program is dead and /var/lock lock file exists
 10298	3       program is not running                        
 10299	4       program or service status is unknown          
 10300	5-99    reserved for future LSB use                   
 10301	100-149 reserved for distribution use                 
 10302	150-199 reserved for application use                  
 10303	200-254 reserved                                      
 10304	
 10305	In the case of init script commands other than "status" (i.e., "start", "stop",
 10306	"restart", "reload", and "force-reload"), the init script must return an exit
 10307	status of zero if the action described by the argument has been successful.
 10308	Otherwise, the exit status shall be non-zero, as defined below. In addition to
 10309	straightforward success, the following situations are also to be considered
 10310	successful:
 10311	
 10312	  * restarting a service (instead of reloading it) with the "force-reload"
 10313	    argument
 10314	   
 10315	  * running "start" on a service already running
 10316	   
 10317	  * running "stop" on a service already stopped or not running
 10318	   
 10319	  * running "restart" on a service already stopped or not running
 10320	   
 10321	 
 10322	
 10323	In case of an error, while processing any init script action except for
 10324	"status", the init script must print an error message and return one of the
 10325	following non-zero exit status codes.
 10326	
 10327	1       generic or unspecified error (current practice)
 10328	2       invalid or excess argument(s)                  
 10329	3       unimplemented feature (for example, "reload")  
 10330	4       user had insufficient privilege                
 10331	5       program is not installed                       
 10332	6       program is not configured                      
 10333	7       program is not running                         
 10334	8-99    reserved for future LSB use                    
 10335	100-149 reserved for distribution use                  
 10336	150-199 reserved for application use                   
 10337	200-254 reserved                                       
 10338	
 10339	Error and status messages should be printed with the logging functions such as
 10340	log_failure_msg and so on. Scripts may write to standard error or standard
 10341	output, but implementations need not present text written to standard error/
 10342	output to the user or do anything else with it.
 10343	
 10344	Since init files may be run manually by a system administrator with
 10345	non-standard environment variable values for PATH, USER, LOGNAME, etc. init
 10346	files must not depend on the values of these environment variables. They should
 10347	set them to some known/default values if they are needed. 
 10348	
 10349	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 10350	
 10351	Comment conventions for init scripts
 10352	
 10353	LSB applications which need to execute script(s) at bootup and/or shutdown may
 10354	provide one or more init.d files. These files are installed by the
 10355	install_initd program described below, which copies it into a standard
 10356	directory and makes whatever other adjustments (creation of symlinks, creation
 10357	of entries in a database, etc.) are necessary so that the script can be run at
 10358	boot-time. [3]
 10359	
 10360	In the init.d file, information about the shell script shall be delimited by
 10361	the lines "### BEGIN INIT INFO" and "### END INIT INFO". These delimiter lines
 10362	may containg trailing whitespace, which shall be ignored. Inside this block
 10363	there shall be lines of the form "# {keyword}: [arg1] [arg2] ...". (All lines
 10364	inside this block start with a hash ('#') character in the first column, so
 10365	that shell treats them as comments.) There must be exactly one space character
 10366	between "#" and the keyword.[4] The following keywords, with their arguments
 10367	are defined in this specification:
 10368	
 10369	        # Provides: boot_facility_1 [ boot_facility_2 ...]
 10370	        # Required-Start: boot_facility_1 [ boot_facility_2 ...]
 10371	        # Required-Stop: boot_facility_1 [ boot_facility_2 ...]
 10372	        # Should-Start: boot_facility_1 [ boot_facility_2 ...]
 10373	        # Should-Stop: boot_facility_1 [ boot_facility_2 ...]
 10374	        # Default-Start: run_level_1 [ run_level_2 ...]
 10375	        # Default-Stop: run_level_1 [ run_level_2 ...]
 10376	        # Short-Description: short_description
 10377	        # Description: multiline_description
 10378	
 10379	Additional keywords may be defined in future LSB specifications. Distributions
 10380	may define local extensions by using the prefix "X-[distribution name]" --- for
 10381	example, "X-RedHat-foobardecl", or "X-Debian-xyzzydecl".
 10382	
 10383	An init.d shell script may declare using the "Required-Start: " header that it
 10384	must not be run until certain boot facilities are provided. This information is
 10385	used by the installation tool or the boot-time boot-script execution facility
 10386	to assure that init scripts are run in the correct order. When an init script
 10387	is run with a "start" argument, the boot facility or facilities specified in
 10388	the "Provides" header shall be considered present, and hence init scripts which
 10389	require those boot facilities would then be eligble to be run. When an init
 10390	script is run with a "stop" argument, the boot facilities specified in the
 10391	"Provides" header are considered no longer present. There are naming
 10392	conventions for boot facilities and system facilities, as described in a
 10393	following section.
 10394	
 10395	Similarly, the "Required-Stop:" header defines which facilities must still be
 10396	available during the shutdown of that service. Hence, the init script system
 10397	should avoid stopping shell scripts which provide those facilities until this
 10398	shell script is stopped.
 10399	
 10400	The "Should-Start:" header defines which facilities if present should be
 10401	started before this service. This allows for weak dependencies which do not
 10402	cause the service to fail if a facility is not available. But may cause reduced
 10403	functionality of the service. Compliant applications should not rely on the
 10404	existence of this feature.
 10405	
 10406	The "Should-Stop:" header defines which facilities should be still available
 10407	during the shutdown of that service.
 10408	
 10409	The "Default-Start" and "Default-Stop" headers define which run levels should
 10410	by default run the script with a start or stop argument, respectively, to start
 10411	or stop the services controlled by the init script.
 10412	
 10413	The "Short-Description" and "Description" header fields are used to provide
 10414	text which describes the actions of the init script. The "short_description"
 10415	shall be a relatively short, pithy description of the init script, where as the
 10416	"multiline_description" can be a much longer piece of text that may span
 10417	mulitple lines. In a multiline description, each continuation line must begin
 10418	with a '#' followed by tab character or a '#' followed by at least two space
 10419	characters. The multiline description is terminated by the first line that does
 10420	not match this criteria.
 10421	
 10422	The comment conventions described in this session are only required for use by
 10423	LSB-compliant applications; system init scripts as provided by LSB-compliant
 10424	run-time environments are not required to use the scheme outlined here.
 10425	
 10426	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 10427	
 10428	Installation and removal of init.d files
 10429	
 10430	An init.d file is installed by copying it into /etc/init.d (which may be a
 10431	symlink to another location). This can be done by the package installer. During
 10432	the package's postinstall script, the program "/usr/lib/lsb/install_initd"
 10433	configures the distribution's boot script system to call the package's init.d
 10434	file at the appropriate time.
 10435	
 10436	The install_initd program takes a single argument, the pathanme to the /etc/
 10437	init.d file. For example:
 10438	
 10439	        /usr/lib/lsb/install_initd /etc/init.d/example.com-coffeed
 10440	
 10441	The install_initd program shall return an exit status of zero if the init.d
 10442	file has been successfully installed or if the the init.d file was already
 10443	installed. If the required boot facilities cannot be fulfilled an exit status
 10444	of one shall be returned and the init.d file shall not be installed.
 10445	
 10446	When a software package is removed, the package's preuninstall script shall
 10447	call /usr/lib/lsb/remove_initd and pass the pathname to the /etc/init.d file.
 10448	The package manager is still responsible for removing the /etc/init.d file; the
 10449	remove_initd program is provided in case the distribution needs to clean up any
 10450	other modifications in the distribution's boot script system that might have
 10451	been made by the install_initd program. For example:
 10452	
 10453	        /usr/lib/lsb/remove_initd /etc/init.d/example.com-coffeed
 10454	
 10455	The remove_initd program shall return an exit status of zero if the init.d file
 10456	has been successfully removed or if the the init.d file is not installed. If
 10457	another init.d file which depends on a boot facility provided by this init.d
 10458	file is installed, an exit status of one shall be returned and the init.d file
 10459	shall remained installed.
 10460	
 10461	There should be a tool available to the user (e.g., RedHat's chkconfig) which
 10462	can be used by the system administrator to easily manipulate at which init
 10463	levels a particular init.d script is started or stopped. This specification
 10464	currently does not specify such an interface, however.
 10465	
 10466	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 10467	
 10468	Run Levels
 10469	
 10470	 The following run levels are specified for use by the "Default-Start:" and
 10471	"Default-Stop:" specifiers as defined by the section Comment conventions for
 10472	init scripts>. Many LSB run-time environments commonly use these run level
 10473	definitions, and in the absence of other considerations, providers of run-time
 10474	environments are strongly encouraged to follow this convention to provide
 10475	consistency for system administrators who need to work with multiple
 10476	distributions. However, it is not required that LSB-compliant run-time
 10477	environments use these run levels; the distribution-provided install_initd
 10478	script may map the run levels specified below to whatever
 10479	distribution-specified run levels are most appropriate. 
 10480	
 10481	0 halt                                                    
 10482	1 single user mode                                        
 10483	2 multiuser with no network services exported             
 10484	3 normal/full multiuser                                   
 10485	4 reserved for local use, default is normal/full multiuser
 10486	5 multiuser with xdm or equivalent                        
 10487	6 reboot                                                  
 10488	
 10489	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 10490	
 10491	Facility names
 10492	
 10493	Boot facilities are used to indicate dependencies in init scripts, as defined
 10494	in a previous section. Facility names that begin with a dollar sign ('$') are
 10495	system facility names, defined by the LSB, and MUST be provided by
 10496	distributions. [5] LSB applications must not provide facilities that begin with
 10497	a dollar sign. This document defines the following facility names:
 10498	
 10499	$local_fs  all local filesystems are mounted                                   
 10500	$network   low level networking (ethernet card; may imply PCMCIA running)      
 10501	$named     daemons which may provide hostname resolution (if present) are      
 10502	           running                                                             
 10503	$portmap   daemons providing SunRPC/ONCRPC portmapping service[6] (if present) 
 10504	           are running                                                         
 10505	$remote_fs all remote filesystems are mounted[7].                              
 10506	$syslog    system logger is operational                                        
 10507	$time      the system time has been set [8]                                    
 10508	
 10509	Other (non-system) facilities may be defined by other LSB applications. These
 10510	facilities shall be named using the same conventions defined for naming init.d
 10511	script names. Commonly, the facility provided by an LSB application init.d
 10512	script will have the same name as the name assigned to the init.d script.
 10513	
 10514	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 10515	
 10516	Script names
 10517	
 10518	Since the init.d scripts must live in a single directory, they must come from a
 10519	single namespace. Three means of assigning names from this namespace are
 10520	available:
 10521	
 10522	  * Assigned namespace. This namespace consists of names which only use the
 10523	    character set [a-z0-9]. This space is desirable for scripts which system
 10524	    administrators may often wish to run manually: e.g., "/etc/init.d/named
 10525	    restart" In order to avoid conflicts these init.d names must be reserved
 10526	    through the Linux Assigned Names and Numbers Authority (LANANA).
 10527	    Information about the LANANA may be found at www.lanana.org.
 10528	   
 10529	    Commonly used names shall be reserved in advance; developers for projects
 10530	    should be encouraged to reserve names from LANANA, so that each
 10531	    distribution can use the same name, and to avoid conflicts with other
 10532	    projects.
 10533	   
 10534	  * Hierarchical namespace. This namespace consists of scripts names which look
 10535	    like this: [hier1]-[hier2]-...-[name], where name is again taken the
 10536	    character set [a-z0-9], and where there may be one or more [hier-n]
 10537	    components. [hier1] may either be an LSB provider name assigned by the
 10538	    LANANA, or it may be owners' DNS name in lower case, with at least one '.'
 10539	    (e.g., "debian.org", "staroffice.sun.com"). The LSB provider name assigned
 10540	    by LANANA must only consist of the ASCII characters [a-z0-9].
 10541	   
 10542	  * Reserved namespace. This namespace consists of script names which begin
 10543	    with the character '_', and is reserved for distribution use only. This
 10544	    namespace should be used for core packages only, and in general use of this
 10545	    namespace is highly discouraged.  
 10546	   
 10547	In general, if a package or some system function is likely to be used on
 10548	multiple systems, the package developers or the distribution SHOULD get a
 10549	registered name through LANANA, and distributions should strive to use the same
 10550	name whenever possible. For applications which may not be "core" or may not be
 10551	commonly installed, the hierarchical namespace may be more appropriate. An
 10552	advantage to the hierarchical namespace is that there is no need to consult
 10553	with the LANANA before obtaining an assigned name.
 10554	
 10555	Short names are highly desirable, since many system administrators like to use
 10556	them to manually start and stop services. Given this, they should be
 10557	standardized on a per-package basis. This is the rationale behind having a
 10558	LANANA organization to assign these names. The LANANA may be called upon to
 10559	handle other namespace issues, such as package/prerequisites naming (which is
 10560	essential to making prerequisites to work correctly).
 10561	
 10562	-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
 10563	
 10564	Init script Functions
 10565	
 10566	Each LSB-compliant init.d script must source the file /lib/lsb/init-functions.
 10567	This file must cause the following shell script commands to be defined. This
 10568	can be done either by adding a directory to the PATH variable which defines
 10569	these commands, or by defining sh aliases. While the distribution-provided
 10570	aliases may choose to use bash extensions (at the distribution's option), the
 10571	LSB init.d files themselves should only depend in /bin/sh features as defined
 10572	by POSIX.2.
 10573	
 10574	                This runs the specified program as a daemon. start_daemon will 
 10575	start_daemon    check to see if there is a program named "daemon" already      
 10576	[-f] [-n        running. If so, it will not start another copy of the daemon   
 10577	nicelevel] [-p  unless the -f option is given. The -n option specifies a nice  
 10578	pidfile]        level. See nice(1). start_daemon should return the LSB defined 
 10579	pathname [args] exit status codes. It shall return 0 if the program has been   
 10580	                successfully started or is running and not 0 otherwise.        
 10581	                This stops the specified program. The program is found using   
 10582	                the algorithm given by pidofproc. If a signal is specified,    
 10583	                using the -signal_name or -signal_number syntaxes specified by 
 10584	killproc [-p    the kill command, the program is sent that signal. Otherwise, a
 10585	pidfile]        SIGTERM followed by a SIGKILL after some number of seconds is  
 10586	pathname        sent. Compliant applications may use the basename instead of   
 10587	[signal]        the pathname. killproc should return the LSB defined exit      
 10588	                status codes. If called without a signal, it shall return 0 if 
 10589	                the program has been stopped or is not running and not 0       
 10590	                otherwise. If a signal is given, it shall return 0 only if the 
 10591	                program is running.                                            
 10592	                This function returns one or more pid(s) for a particular      
 10593	                daemon. If an entry is found in /var/run/basename.pid, then    
 10594	                that value is returned. If the -p option is used, the given    
 10595	                pidfile is used instead. Compliant applications may use the    
 10596	                basename instead of the pathname. Compliant implementations of 
 10597	                the LSB may attempt other mechanisms for determining the pid   
 10598	pidofproc [-p   (s), although this is not required (and not recommended, since 
 10599	pidfile]        a user can trick startup scripts by creating processes that    
 10600	pathname        appear to be system programs in the process list thus creating 
 10601	                a potential security exposure). Hence, LSB-complaint           
 10602	                applications who wish to use the pidofproc function in their   
 10603	                init scripts must store the pid in /var/run/basename.pid.      
 10604	                pidofproc should return the LSB defined exist status codes for 
 10605	                "status". It shall return 0 if the program is the process is   
 10606	                running and not 0 otherwise.                                   
 10607	log_success_msg This requests the distribution to print a success message. The 
 10608	"message"       message should be relatively short; no more than 60 characters 
 10609	                is highly desirable.                                           
 10610	log_failure_msg This requests the distribution to print a failure message. The 
 10611	"message"       message should be relatively short; no more than 60 characters 
 10612	                is highly desirable.                                           
 10613	log_warning_msg This requests the distribution to print a warning message. The 
 10614	"message"       message should be relatively short; no more than 60 characters 
 10615	                is highly desirable.                                           
 10616	
 10617	Notes
 10618	
 10619	[1]  ISO/IEC 14882: 1998(E) Programming languages --C++                        
 10620	                                                                               
 10621	[2]  Linux Standard Base                                                       
 10622	                                                                               
 10623	[3]  This specification does not require, but is designed to allow, the        
 10624	     development of a system which runs boot scripts in parallel. Hence,       
 10625	     enforced-serialization of scripts is avoided unless it is explicitly      
 10626	     necessary.                                                                
 10627	                                                                               
 10628	[4]  More than one space, or a tab character, indicates the continuation line. 
 10629	                                                                               
 10630	[5]  The dollar sign does not indicate variable expansion as in many Linux     
 10631	     utilities. Starting a facility name with a dollar sign is merely a way of 
 10632	     dividing the namespace between the system and applications.               
 10633	                                                                               
 10634	[6]  as defined in RFC 1833                                                    
 10635	                                                                               
 10636	[7]  In some LSB run-time environments, filesystems such as /usr may be remote.
 10637	     Many applications that require $local_fs will probably require also       
 10638	     require $remote_fs                                                        
 10639	                                                                               
 10640	[8]  i.e., using a network-based time program such as ntp or rdate, or via the 
 10641	     hardware Real Time Clock
